family">A321neo</a> attracts more orders, the sale value of a 737-9 is the same as a 2018 737-8 at $53<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>million.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="737_MAX_10">737 MAX 10</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Boeing_737_MAX&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: 737 MAX 10">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Boeing_737_MAX_10X_rendering.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/2/22/Boeing_737_MAX_10X_rendering.jpeg/220px-Boeing_737_MAX_10X_rendering.jpeg" decoding="async" width="220" height="123" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/2/22/Boeing_737_MAX_10X_rendering.jpeg/330px-Boeing_737_MAX_10X_rendering.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/2/22/Boeing_737_MAX_10X_rendering.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="421" data-file-height="236" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Boeing_737_MAX_10X_rendering.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>737 MAX 10 rendering</div></div></div>\n<p>To compete with the <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A321neo" class="mw-redirect" title="Airbus A321neo">Airbus A321neo</a>, loyal customers, such as <a href="/wiki/Korean_Air" title="Korean Air">Korean Air</a> and United Airlines, pressed Boeing to develop a variant larger than the MAX&#160;9, of which Boeing revealed studies in early 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-AW170310_165-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AW170310-165">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup> As the Airbus A321neo had outsold the MAX&#160;9 five-to-one, the proposed MAX&#160;10 included a larger engine, stronger wings, and telescoping <a href="/wiki/Landing_gear" title="Landing gear">landing gear</a> in mid-2016.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup> In September 2016, it was reported that the variant would be simpler and lower-risk with a modest stretch of 6\xe2\x80\x937&#160;ft (1.83\xe2\x80\x932.13&#160;m) for a length of 143\xe2\x80\x93144&#160;ft (43.6\xe2\x80\x9343.9&#160;m), seating 12\xe2\x80\x9318 more passengers for 192\xe2\x80\x93198 in a dual-class layout or 226-232 for a single class, needing an uprated 31,000&#160;lbf (140&#160;kN) LEAP-1B that could be available by 2019, or 2020, and would likely require a landing-gear modification to move the <a href="/wiki/Rotation_(aeronautics)" title="Rotation (aeronautics)">rotation</a> point slightly <a href="/wiki/Aft" title="Aft">aft</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In October 2016, Boeing\'s board of directors granted authority to offer the stretched variant with two extra fuselage sections forward and aft with a 3,100 nautical miles (3,600&#160;mi; 5,700&#160;km) range reduced from 3,300 nautical miles (3,800&#160;mi; 6,100&#160;km) of the MAX&#160;9.<sup id="cite_ref-AW170310_165-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AW170310-165">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup> In early 2017, Boeing showed a 66&#160;in (1.7&#160;m) stretch to 143 feet (44&#160;m), enabling seating for 230 in a single class or 189 in two-class capacity, compared to 193 in two-class seating for the A321neo. The modest stretch of the MAX&#160;10 enables the aircraft to retain the existing wing, and the Leap 1B engine from the MAX&#160;9 with a trailing-link main landing gear as the only major change.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup> Boeing 737 MAX Vice President and General Manager Keith Leverkuhn said the design had to be frozen in 2018, for a 2020 introduction.<sup id="cite_ref-AW170310_165-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AW170310-165">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Boeing_737_MAX_10_model_ILA_2018.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Boeing_737_MAX_10_model_ILA_2018.png/280px-Boeing_737_MAX_10_model_ILA_2018.png" decoding="async" width="280" height="85" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Boeing_737_MAX_10_model_ILA_2018.png/420px-Boeing_737_MAX_10_model_ILA_2018.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Boeing_737_MAX_10_model_ILA_2018.png/560px-Boeing_737_MAX_10_model_ILA_2018.png 2x" data-file-width="1365" data-file-height="414" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Boeing_737_MAX_10_model_ILA_2018.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>737 MAX 10 model at <a href="/wiki/ILA_Berlin_Air_Show" title="ILA Berlin Air Show">ILA Berlin Air Show</a> 2018</div></div></div>\n<p>Boeing hopes that 737-900 operators and 737 MAX 9 customers like United Airlines, <a href="/wiki/Delta_Air_Lines" title="Delta Air Lines">Delta Air Lines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alaska_Airlines" title="Alaska Airlines">Alaska Airlines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Air_Canada" title="Air Canada">Air Canada</a>, Lion Air, and Chinese airlines will be interested in the new variant.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup> Boeing predicts a 5% lower trip cost and seat cost compared to the A321neo.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Air_Lease_Corporation" title="Air Lease Corporation">Air Lease Corporation</a> wants it a year sooner; its CEO John Pleuger stated "It would have been better to get the first airplane in March 2019, but I don\'t think that\'s possible".<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/AerCap" title="AerCap">AerCap</a> CEO Aengus Kelly is cautious and said the -9 and -10 "will cannibalize each other".<sup id="cite_ref-AW170310_165-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AW170310-165">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The 737 MAX 10 was launched on June 19, 2017, with 240 orders and commitments from more than ten customers.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup> United Airlines will be the largest 737 MAX 10 customer, converting 100 of their 161 orders for the MAX&#160;9 into orders for the MAX&#160;10.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup> Boeing ended the 2017 Paris Air Show with 361 orders and commitments, including 214 conversions, from 16 customers,<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup> including 50 orders from Lion Air.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The variant configuration was firmed up by February 2018,<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup> and by mid-2018, the <a href="/wiki/Critical_design_review" class="mw-redirect" title="Critical design review">critical design review</a> was completed. As of August 2018<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Boeing_737_MAX&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, assembly was underway with a first flight planned for late 2019. The semi-levered landing gear design has a telescoping oleo-pneumatic strut with a down-swinging lever to permit a 9.5 inches (24&#160;cm) taller gear. Driven by the existing retraction system, a shrink-link <a href="/wiki/Mechanical_linkage" class="mw-redirect" title="Mechanical linkage">mechanical linkage</a> mechanism at the top of the leg, inspired by <a href="/wiki/Carrier_aircraft" class="mw-redirect" title="Carrier aircraft">carrier aircraft</a> designs, allows the gear to be drawn in and shortened while being retracted into the existing <a href="/wiki/Wheel_well" class="mw-redirect" title="Wheel well">wheel well</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-AvWeek30aug2018_178-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AvWeek30aug2018-178">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-AvWeek9feb2018_179-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AvWeek9feb2018-179">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup> Entry into service is slated for July 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-Boeing-737MAX10Brochure_180-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Boeing-737MAX10Brochure-180">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On November 22, 2019, Boeing unveiled the first MAX 10 to employees in its Renton factory, Washington, scheduled for the first flight in 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>At the time, 531 MAX 10s were on order, compared to 3,142 Airbus A321neos sold, capable of carrying 244 passengers or to fly up to 4,700&#160;nmi (8,700&#160;km) in its heaviest <a href="/wiki/A321XLR" class="mw-redirect" title="A321XLR">A321XLR</a> variant.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup> The MAX&#160;10 has similar capacity as the A321XLR, but shorter range and much poorer field performance in smaller airports than the A321XLR.<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup>\nIn early 2021, Boeing expected 737 MAX 10 deliveries to start in 2023.<sup id="cite_ref-Flight2feb2021_139-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Flight2feb2021-139">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Boeing_Business_Jet">Boeing Business Jet</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Boeing_737_MAX&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Boeing Business Jet">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The <b>BBJ MAX 8</b> and <b>BBJ MAX 9</b> are proposed <a href="/wiki/Business_jet" title="Business jet">business jet</a> variants of the 737 MAX 8 and 9, with new CFM LEAP-1B engines and advanced winglets providing 13% better fuel burn than the <a href="/wiki/Boeing_Business_Jet" title="Boeing Business Jet">Boeing Business Jet</a>; the BBJ MAX 8 will have a 6,325&#160;nmi (11,710&#160;km) range, and the BBJ MAX 9 a 6,255&#160;nmi (11,580&#160;km) range.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup> The <b>BBJ MAX 7</b> was unveiled in October 2016, with a 7,000&#160;nmi (12,960&#160;km) range and 10% lower operating costs than the original BBJ, while being larger.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup> The BBJ MAX 8 first flew on April 16, 2018, before delivery later the same year, and will have a range of 6,640&#160;nmi (12,300&#160;km) with an auxiliary fuel tank.<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Replacement_airliner">Replacement airliner</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Boeing_737_MAX&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Replacement airliner">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In November 2014, Boeing talked about developing a clean sheet aircraft to replace the 737. The airplane was to have a similar fuselage but made from composite materials developed for the Dreamliner.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup> Boeing also considered a parallel development along with the 757 replacement, similar to the development of the 757 and 767 in the 1970s.<sup id="cite_ref-awnNeo_188-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-awnNeo-188">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Orders_and_deliveries">Orders and deliveries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Boeing_737_MAX&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Orders and deliveries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Boeing_737_MAX_orders_and_deliveries" title="List of Boeing 737 MAX orders and deliveries">List of Boeing 737 MAX orders and deliveries</a></div>\n<p>American Airlines was the first disclosed customer. By November 17, 2011, there were 700 commitments from nine customers, including Lion Air and <a href="/wiki/SMBC_Aviation_Capital" title="SMBC Aviation Capital">SMBC Aviation Capital</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup> By December 2011, the 737 MAX had 948 commitments and firm orders from thirteen customers.<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup> On September 8, 2014, Ryanair agreed to 100 firm orders with 100 options.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup> In January 2017, aircraft leasing company GECAS ordered 75.<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup> By January 2019 the 737 MAX had 5,011 firm orders from 78 identified customers,<sup id="cite_ref-737_O_D_121-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-737_O_D-121">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> with the top three being Southwest Airlines with 280, flydubai with 251, and Lion Air with 251.<sup id="cite_ref-737_O_D_121-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-737_O_D-121">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> The first 737 MAX 8 was delivered to <a href="/wiki/Malindo_Air" title="Malindo Air">Malindo Air</a> on May 16, 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-Flight16may2017_53-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Flight16may2017-53">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Following the groundings in March 2019, Boeing suspended all deliveries of 737 MAX aircraft,<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup> reduced production from 52 to 42 aircraft per month,<sup id="cite_ref-Boeing-20190405_73-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Boeing-20190405-73">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> and on December 16, 2019, announced that production would be suspended from January 2020 to conserve cash and prioritize delivery of the 387 aircraft in storage once recertified.<sup id="cite_ref-Boeing16dec2019_75-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Boeing16dec2019-75">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> At the time of the grounding, the 737 MAX had 4,636 unfilled orders<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup> valued at an estimated $600<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>billion.<sup id="cite_ref-risk_196-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-risk-196">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup> By November 30, 2020, the unfilled orders stood at 4,039 and the backlog at 3,290, after accounting adjustments recognizing orders unlikely to be filled.<sup id="cite_ref-737_O_D_121-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-737_O_D-121">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-backlogNov2020_198-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-backlogNov2020-198">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><br />\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable" style="margin:1em 1em 1em 300; border:1px #aaa solid; font-size:95%; background:#fbf8db;">\n<caption>Boeing 737 MAX orders and deliveries<sup id="cite_ref-O_D_summ_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-O_D_summ-6">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>\n</caption>\n<tbody><tr href="#cite_note-MaxOrders2020-201">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-203"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-203">^</a></b></span> <span .25em .25em;">&#8195;</span>Deliveries</p><div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<p>As of March&#160;31,&#32;2021<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Boeing_737_MAX&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-O_D_summ_6-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-O_D_summ-6">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><br />\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Accidents_and_incidents">Accidents and incidents</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Boeing_737_MAX&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Accidents and incidents">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Boeing_737_MAX_grounded_aircraft_near_Boeing_Field,_April_2019.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Boeing_737_MAX_grounded_aircraft_near_Boeing_Field%2C_April_2019.jpg/220px-Boeing_737_MAX_grounded_aircraft_near_Boeing_Field%2C_April_2019.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Boeing_737_MAX_grounded_aircraft_near_Boeing_Field%2C_April_2019.jpg/330px-Boeing_737_MAX_grounded_aircraft_near_Boeing_Field%2C_April_2019.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Boeing_737_MAX_grounded_aircraft_near_Boeing_Field%2C_April_2019.jpg/440px-Boeing_737_MAX_grounded_aircraft_near_Boeing_Field%2C_April_2019.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3452" data-file-height="2298" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Boeing_737_MAX_grounded_aircraft_near_Boeing_Field,_April_2019.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Grounded 737 MAX aircraft at <a href="/wiki/Boeing_Field" title="Boeing Field">Boeing Field</a> in Seattle</div></div></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Boeing_737_MAX_groundings" title="Boeing 737 MAX groundings">Boeing 737 MAX groundings</a></div>\n<p>Between March 2017 and March 2019, the global fleet of 387 aircraft operated 500,000 flights and experienced two fatal accidents, having an accident rate of four accidents per million flights when it was grounded. The previous Boeing 737 generations averaged 0.2 accidents per one million flights.<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Lion_Air_Flight_610">Lion Air Flight 610</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Boeing_737_MAX&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Lion Air Flight 610">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Lion_Air_Flight_610" title="Lion Air Flight 610">Lion Air Flight 610</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Lion_Air_Boeing_737-MAX8_PK-LQP.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Lion_Air_Boeing_737-MAX8_PK-LQP.jpg/220px-Lion_Air_Boeing_737-MAX8_PK-LQP.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Lion_Air_Boeing_737-MAX8_PK-LQP.jpg/330px-Lion_Air_Boeing_737-MAX8_PK-LQP.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Lion_Air_Boeing_737-MAX8_PK-LQP.jpg/440px-Lion_Air_Boeing_737-MAX8_PK-LQP.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4912" data-file-height="3264" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Lion_Air_Boeing_737-MAX8_PK-LQP.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Lion_Air" title="Lion Air">Lion Air</a>\'s 737 MAX 8, reg. PK-LQP, the airframe involved in the JT610 accident</div></div></div>\n<p>On October 29, 2018, <a href="/wiki/Lion_Air_Flight_610" title="Lion Air Flight 610">Lion Air Flight 610</a>, 737 MAX 8 registration PK-LQP, plunged into the <a href="/wiki/Java_Sea" title="Java Sea">Java Sea</a> 13 minutes after takeoff from <a href="/wiki/Soekarno%E2%80%93Hatta_International_Airport" title="Soekarno\xe2\x80\x93Hatta International Airport">Soekarno\xe2\x80\x93Hatta International Airport</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jakarta" title="Jakarta">Jakarta</a>, Indonesia. The flight was a scheduled domestic flight to <a href="/wiki/Depati_Amir_Airport" title="Depati Amir Airport">Depati Amir Airport</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pangkal_Pinang" title="Pangkal Pinang">Pangkal Pinang</a>, Indonesia. All 189 people on board died. This was the first fatal aviation accident and first hull loss of a 737 MAX. The aircraft had been delivered to Lion Air two months earlier.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc._Howc_205-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc._Howc-205">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup> People familiar with the investigation reported that during a flight piloted by a different crew on the day before the crash, the same aircraft experienced a similar malfunction but an extra pilot sitting in the cockpit jumpseat correctly diagnosed the problem and told the crew how to disable the malfunctioning MCAS flight-control system.<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup>  Indonesia\'s <a href="/wiki/Komite_Nasional_Keselamatan_Transportasi" class="mw-redirect" title="Komite Nasional Keselamatan Transportasi">National Transportation Safety Committee</a> released its final report into the accident on October 25, 2019,<sup id="cite_ref-Final_208-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Final-208">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup> attributing the crash to the MCAS pushing the aircraft into a <a href="/wiki/Descent_(aeronautics)#Dives" title="Descent (aeronautics)">dive</a> due to data from a faulty angle-of-attack sensor. Following the Lion Air crash, Boeing issued an operational manual guidance, advising airlines on how to address erroneous cockpit readings.<sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethiopian_Airlines_Flight_302">Ethiopian Airlines Flight 302</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Boeing_737_MAX&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Ethiopian Airlines Flight 302">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Ethiopian_Airlines_Flight_302" title="Ethiopian Airlines Flight 302">Ethiopian Airlines Flight 302</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ethiopian_Airlines_ET-AVJ_takeoff.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Ethiopian_Airlines_ET-AVJ_takeoff.jpg/220px-Ethiopian_Airlines_ET-AVJ_takeoff.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Ethiopian_Airlines_ET-AVJ_takeoff.jpg/330px-Ethiopian_Airlines_ET-AVJ_takeoff.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Ethiopian_Airlines_ET-AVJ_takeoff.jpg/440px-Ethiopian_Airlines_ET-AVJ_takeoff.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3210" data-file-height="2140" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ethiopian_Airlines_ET-AVJ_takeoff.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Ethiopian_Airlines" title="Ethiopian Airlines">Ethiopian Airlines</a> 737 MAX 8 reg. ET-AVJ, the airframe involved in the ET302 accident</div></div></div>\n<p>On March 10, 2019, <a href="/wiki/Ethiopian_Airlines_Flight_302" title="Ethiopian Airlines Flight 302">Ethiopian Airlines Flight 302</a>, 737 MAX 8 registration ET-AVJ, crashed approximately six minutes after takeoff from <a href="/wiki/Addis_Ababa_Bole_International_Airport" title="Addis Ababa Bole International Airport">Addis Ababa</a>, Ethiopia,<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup> on a scheduled flight to <a href="/wiki/Jomo_Kenyatta_International_Airport" title="Jomo Kenyatta International Airport">Nairobi</a>, Kenya,<sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">&#91;207&#93;</a></sup> killing all 149 passengers and 8 crew members on board. The aircraft was four months old at the time.<sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup> The cause of the crash was initially unclear, though the aircraft\'s vertical speed after takeoff was reported to be unstable.<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup> Evidence retrieved on the crash site suggests, that at the time of the crash, the aircraft was configured to dive, similar to Lion Air Flight 610.<sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">&#91;210&#93;</a></sup> On April 4, Ethiopian transport minister <a href="/wiki/Dagmawit_Moges" title="Dagmawit Moges">Dagmawit Moges</a> stated, that the crew "performed all the procedures repeatedly provided by the manufacturer[,] but was not able to control the aircraft."<sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">&#91;211&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The subsequent findings in the Ethiopian Airlines crash and the Lion Air crash led to the global 737 MAX groundings. On August 19, 2019, <i>Forbes</i> estimated that the 737 MAX would not resume service before 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-Leap_216-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Leap-216">&#91;212&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Specifications">Specifications</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span
